          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;

        }

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

            Issue 

1272967

: 

Security: UAF in P2PSocketTcpServer::DoAccept

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





P2PSocketTcpServer::DoAccept would call HandleAcceptResult if the result of Accept is not equal to net::ERR_IO_PENDING [1]. And HandleAcceptResult subsequently calls OnError if the result is negative [2]. This will destroy the P2PSocketTcpServer instance by erasing it from a flat_map in P2PSocketManager [3]. However, DoAccept continues to access class members in a while loop after its destruction, which leads to UAF.



<span class="line"><!---->P2PSocketTcpServer::DoAccept would call HandleAcceptResult if the result of Accept is not equal to net::ERR_IO_PENDING [1]. And HandleAcceptResult subsequently calls OnError if the result is negative [2]. This will destroy the P2PSocketTcpServer instance by erasing it from a flat_map in P2PSocketManager [3]. However, DoAccept continues to access class members in a while loop after its destruction, which leads to UAF.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





void P2PSocketTcpServer::DoAccept() {



<span class="line"><!---->void P2PSocketTcpServer::DoAccept() {<!----></span>



<br>





  while (true) {



<span class="line"><!---->  while (true) {<!----></span>



<br>





    int result = socket_->Accept(&accept_socket_, accept_callback_);



<span class="line"><!---->    int result = socket_-&gt;Accept(&amp;accept_socket_, accept_callback_);<!----></span>



<br>





    if (result == net::ERR_IO_PENDING) {



<span class="line"><!---->    if (result == net::ERR_IO_PENDING) {<!----></span>



<br>





      break;



<span class="line"><!---->      break;<!----></span>



<br>





    } else {



<span class="line"><!---->    } else {<!----></span>



<br>





      HandleAcceptResult(result);    // ======> [1]



<span class="line"><!---->      HandleAcceptResult(result);    // ======&gt; [1]<!----></span>



<br>





    }



<span class="line"><!---->    }<!----></span>



<br>





  }



<span class="line"><!---->  }<!----></span>



<br>





}



<span class="line"><!---->}<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





void P2PSocketTcpServer::HandleAcceptResult(int result) {



<span class="line"><!---->void P2PSocketTcpServer::HandleAcceptResult(int result) {<!----></span>



<br>





  if (result < 0) {



<span class="line"><!---->  if (result &lt; 0) {<!----></span>



<br>





    if (result != net::ERR_IO_PENDING)



<span class="line"><!---->    if (result != net::ERR_IO_PENDING)<!----></span>



<br>





      OnError();                     // ======> [2]



<span class="line"><!---->      OnError();                     // ======&gt; [2]<!----></span>



<br>





    return;



<span class="line"><!---->    return;<!----></span>



<br>





  }



<span class="line"><!---->  }<!----></span>



<br>





  // ...



<span class="line"><!---->  // ...<!----></span>



<br>





}



<span class="line"><!---->}<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





void P2PSocketManager::DestroySocket(P2PSocket* socket) {



<span class="line"><!---->void P2PSocketManager::DestroySocket(P2PSocket* socket) {<!----></span>



<br>





  auto iter = sockets_.find(socket);



<span class="line"><!---->  auto iter = sockets_.find(socket);<!----></span>



<br>





  DCHECK(iter != sockets_.end());



<span class="line"><!---->  DCHECK(iter != sockets_.end());<!----></span>



<br>





  sockets_.erase(iter);              // ======> [3]



<span class="line"><!---->  sockets_.erase(iter);              // ======&gt; [3]<!----></span>



<br>





}



<span class="line"><!---->}<!----></span>

VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





Chrome Version: 96.0.4664.45 (stable)



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: 96.0.4664.45 (stable)<!----></span>

<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





I think the quick way to demonstrate the UAF is to trigger ENFILE (Too many open files) error on Linux platform by spawning lots of tcp connections to P2PSocketTcpServer.



<span class="line"><!---->I think the quick way to demonstrate the UAF is to trigger ENFILE (Too many open files) error on Linux platform by spawning lots of tcp connections to P2PSocketTcpServer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. Apply the patch.diff. This simulates the compromised renderer to send mojo request to setup a P2PSocketTcpServer. (It seems that we can't do it through mojo JS because the mojo call 'CreateSocket' requires native parameters)



<span class="line"><!---->1. Apply the patch.diff. This simulates the compromised renderer to send mojo request to setup a P2PSocketTcpServer. (It seems that we can't do it through mojo JS because the mojo call 'CreateSocket' requires native parameters)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





2. Setup a HTTPServer and navigate to poc.html



<span class="line"><!---->2. Setup a HTTPServer and navigate to poc.html<!----></span>



<br>





python -m SimpleHTTPServer 8000



<span class="line"><!---->python -m SimpleHTTPServer 8000<!----></span>



<br>





./chrome 



<span class="line"><!---->./chrome <!----></span>





http://localhost:8000/poc.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://localhost:8000/poc.html"><!---->http://localhost:8000/poc.html<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





3. Run spawn_nc.sh which simply uses 'nc' command to establish tcp connections to P2PSocketTcpServer. When the number of opened sockets hits the system limit, Accept would return ERR_INSUFFICIENT_RESOURCES as result which triggers the UAF.



<span class="line"><!---->3. Run spawn_nc.sh which simply uses 'nc' command to establish tcp connections to P2PSocketTcpServer. When the number of opened sockets hits the system limit, Accept would return ERR_INSUFFICIENT_RESOURCES as result which triggers the UAF.<!----></span>



<br>





/bin/bash ./spawn_nc.sh



<span class="line"><!---->/bin/bash ./spawn_nc.sh<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





NOTE:



<span class="line"><!---->NOTE:<!----></span>



<br>





I noticed that the buggy code was deleted in 



<span class="line"><!---->I noticed that the buggy code was deleted in <!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3229278



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3229278"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/3229278<!----></a>





 , but the code still exists in currently official stable version (96.0.4664.45).



<span class="line"><!----> , but the code still exists in currently official stable version (96.0.4664.45).<!----></span>

The asan log indicates the reachability of the buggy code:



<span class="line"><!---->The asan log indicates the reachability of the buggy code:<!----></span>



<br>





Render side sends a `CreateSocket` mojo request to P2PSocketManager which lives in the Network service. The first parameter `P2PSocketType` specifies the type of socket to be created, which is a P2PSocketTcpServer in this case.



<span class="line"><!---->Render side sends a `CreateSocket` mojo request to P2PSocketManager which lives in the Network service. The first parameter `P2PSocketType` specifies the type of socket to be created, which is a P2PSocketTcpServer in this case.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The purpose of this patch is only to simulate a compromised renderer to send the mojo request. On current stable version of chrome, this bug can be exploited for sandbox escaping.



<span class="line"><!---->The purpose of this patch is only to simulate a compromised renderer to send the mojo request. On current stable version of chrome, this bug can be exploited for sandbox escaping.<!----></span>

Thanks for explaining. So if an attacker has compromised the renderer process, this bug could be used by the attacker to also compromise the browser process?



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks for explaining. So if an attacker has compromised the renderer process, this bug could be used by the attacker to also compromise the browser process?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'm not familiar with this code, but to me, it seems the conceptually simplest fix would be to delete all support for TCP server sockets from the mojo api. Disabling CreateServerTcpSocket (making it always return null) would have about the same effect.



<span class="line"><!---->I'm not familiar with this code, but to me, it seems the conceptually simplest fix would be to delete all support for TCP server sockets from the mojo api. Disabling CreateServerTcpSocket (making it always return null) would have about the same effect.<!----></span>

Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
